Use Of Estimates|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|Use of EstimatesThe preparation of financial statements in conformity with U.S. GAAP requires management to make estimates and assumptions that affect the reported amounts of assets and liabilities and disclosures of contingent assets and liabilities at the date of the financial statements and the reported amounts of revenue and expenses during the reporting period. Actual results could differ materially from our estimates. On an ongoing basis, we evaluate our estimates, including those related to revenue recognition, cash equivalents and marketable securities, accounts receivable, inventories, income taxes, goodwill, stock-based compensation, litigation, investigation and settlement costs, restructuring and other charges, and other contingencies. The inputs into our judgments and estimates consider the economic implications of COVID-19. These estimates are based on historical facts and various other assumptions that we believe are reasonable.|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-

  Use Of Estimates|c-1|-|-|-|-|-|-|Use of EstimatesThe preparation of financial statements in conformity with U.S. GAAP requires management to make estimates and assumptions that affect the reported amounts of assets and liabilities and disclosures of contingent assets and liabilities at the date of the financial statements and the reported amounts of revenue and expenses during the reporting period. Actual results could differ materially from our estimates. On an ongoing basis, we evaluate our estimates, including those related to revenue recognition, cash equivalents and marketable securities, accounts receivable, inventories, income taxes, goodwill, stock-based compensation, litigation, investigation and settlement costs, restructuring and other charges, and other contingencies. The inputs into our judgments and estimates consider the economic implications of COVID-19. These estimates are based on historical facts and various other assumptions that we believe are reasonable.|-|-|-

@CONCEPT: us-gaap:UseOfEstimates
@VALUE: Use of EstimatesThe preparation of financial statements in conformity with U.S. GAAP requires management to make estimates and assumptions that affect the reported amounts of assets and liabilities and disclosures of contingent assets and liabilities at the date of the financial statements and the reported amounts of revenue and expenses during the reporting period. Actual results could differ materially from our estimates. On an ongoing basis, we evaluate our estimates, including those related to revenue recognition, cash equivalents and marketable securities, accounts receivable, inventories, income taxes, goodwill, stock-based compensation, litigation, investigation and settlement costs, restructuring and other charges, and other contingencies. The inputs into our judgments and estimates consider the economic implications of COVID-19. These estimates are based on historical facts and various other assumptions that we believe are reasonable.

- Current Liabilities + Non-Current Liabilities + Equity = Total Liabilities and Equity

@SEC: ITEM_1A_RISK_FACTORS
@SECTION_TITLE: Risk Factors

@TEXT_REF: Other than the risk factors listed below, there have been no material changes from the risk factors previously described under Item 1A of our Annual Report on Form 10-K for the fiscal year ended January 31, 2021.|tb-1

@TEXT_REF: Before you buy our common stock, you should know that making such an investment involves some risks including, but not limited to, the risks described in Item 1A of our Annual Report on Form 10-K for the fiscal year ended January 31, 2021. Additionally, any one of those risks could harm our business, financial condition and results of operations, which could cause our stock price to decline. Additional risks and uncertainties not presently known to us or that we currently deem immaterial may also impair our business operations.|tb-1

@TEXT_REF: The COVID-19 pandemic continues to impact our business and could materially adversely affect our financial condition and results of operations.|tb-1

@TEXT_REF: COVID-19 has spread worldwide, resulting in government authorities implementing numerous measures to try to contain the disease, such as travel bans and restrictions, quarantines, shelter-in-place orders and shutdowns. These measures have impacted, and may further impact, our workforce and operations, the operations of our customers and our partners, and those of our respective vendors and suppliers (including our subcontractors and third-party contract manufacturers). Our critical business operations, including our headquarters, most of our finished goods inventory and many of our key suppliers, are located in regions which have been impacted by COVID-19. Our customers and suppliers worldwide have also been affected and may continue to be affected by COVID-19 related restrictions and closures.|tb-1

@TEXT_REF: The COVID-19 pandemic continues to evolve and affect our business and financial results and it has increased the duration and impact of economic and demand uncertainty. In the first quarter of fiscal year 2022, our Gaming and Data Center market platforms benefited from stronger demand as people continue to work, learn, and play from home. In Professional Visualization, notebook workstations continue to benefit from work-from-home trends and desktop workstations have started to recover as employees return onsite in certain markets.|tb-1

@EXAMPLE_EXTRACTION
Example of how to extract and format data from this document:

```python
# Extract revenue information for specific period with hierarchy awareness
def extract_revenue(document, context_code):
    # Find the Revenue section
    revenue_section = find_section(document, '<Revenue>')

    # Extract all line items with their context codes
    revenue_data = {}
    totals = {}
    parent_child_map = {}

    # First pass: collect all items and identify parent-child relationships
    for line in revenue_section:
        if context_code in line.split('|')[1].strip():
            columns = line.split('|')
            raw_item_name = columns[0].strip()

            # Parse hierarchy information
            if raw_item_name.startswith('@TOTAL:'):
                # This is a total item
                item_name = raw_item_name.replace('@TOTAL:', '').strip()
                is_total = True
                level = 0  # Top level
            elif raw_item_name.startswith('@SUBTOTAL:'):
                # This is a subtotal item
                item_name = raw_item_name.replace('@SUBTOTAL:', '').strip()
                is_total = True
                level = 1  # Mid level
            elif '@CHILD_OF:' in raw_item_name:
                # This is a child item, extract its parent
                parts = raw_item_name.split('@CHILD_OF:')
                item_name = parts[0].replace('↳', '').strip()
                parent_name = parts[1].strip()
                parent_child_map[item_name] = parent_name
                is_total = False
                level = 2  # Child level
            else:
                # Regular item
                item_name = raw_item_name.strip()
                is_total = False
                level = 1  # Base level

            # Find the value corresponding to the context code
            value = get_value_for_context(columns, context_code)

            # Store with hierarchy information
            if is_total:
                totals[item_name] = {
                    'value': value,
                    'level': level,
                    'components': []  # Will be filled in second pass
                }
            else:
                revenue_data[item_name] = {
                    'value': value,
                    'level': level,
                    'parent': parent_child_map.get(item_name)
                }

    # Second pass: associate children with their parent totals
    for item_name, item_data in revenue_data.items():
        parent = item_data.get('parent')
        if parent and parent in totals:
            totals[parent]['components'].append(item_name)

    # Combine the data structures
    result = {
        'line_items': revenue_data,
        'totals': totals,
        # Include verification formulas
        'verify': {
            'sum_components': 'Sum of all components should equal the total',
            'formula': 'Total_Revenue = Product_Revenue + Service_Revenue + Other_Revenue'
        }
    }
    return result
```

Example hierarchical data format for extraction:

```json
{
  "line_items": {
    "Product_Revenue": {
      "value": 72480,
      "level": 1,
      "parent": "Total_Revenue"
    },
    "Service_Revenue": {
      "value": 16320,
      "level": 1,
      "parent": "Total_Revenue"
    },
    "Automotive_Revenue": {
      "value": 52300,
      "level": 2,
      "parent": "Product_Revenue"
    },
    "Energy_Revenue": {
      "value": 20180,
      "level": 2,
      "parent": "Product_Revenue"
    }
  },
  "totals": {
    "Total_Revenue": {
      "value": 88800,
      "level": 0,
      "components": ["Product_Revenue", "Service_Revenue"],
      "contexts": {
        "c-1": 88800,           // Using short code
        "FY2023": 88800,        // Using semantic code
        "Consolidated_2023": 88800  // Using segment information
      }
    },
    "Product_Revenue": {
      "value": 72480,
      "level": 1,
      "components": ["Automotive_Revenue", "Energy_Revenue"]
    }
  },
  "verify": {
    "equations": [
      "Total_Revenue = Product_Revenue + Service_Revenue",
      "Product_Revenue = Automotive_Revenue + Energy_Revenue"
    ],
    "verified": true
  },
  "metadata": {
    "statement_type": "Income_Statement",
    "period": "FY2023",
    "hierarchical": true
  }
}
```

Note: This hierarchical structure makes parent-child relationships explicit, enabling accurate calculation and validation of totals. The hierarchy levels indicate:
- Level 0: Main totals (like Total Revenue)
- Level 1: Major categories (like Product Revenue)
- Level 2: Subcategories (like Automotive Revenue)

You can use either the numeric short codes (c-1, c-2) or the semantic codes (FY2023, BS_2023_12_31) to access context values. The semantic codes are more descriptive and self-explanatory.
